Time Model Statistics

  • DB Time represents total time in user calls
  • DB CPU represents CPU time of foreground processes
  • Total CPU Time represents foreground and background processes
  • Statistics including the word "background" measure background process time, therefore do not contribute to the DB time statistic
  • Ordered by % of DB time in descending order, followed by Statistic Name

1)*24 + to_number(to_char(begin_interval_time + 0, 'HH24')) hour_id, cpu_time, buffer_gets, executions from (select v1.* from ( select snap_id, dbid, min_inst_num, sql_id, plan_hash_value, cpu_time, buffer_gets, executions, con_dbid from (select snap_id, dbid, min_inst_num, sql_id, plan_hash_value, cpu_time, buffer_gets, executions, con_dbid, row_number() over(partition by dbid, snap_id order by(cpu_time + buffer_gets * 10000) desc) as within_snap_rnk from (select /*+ cardinality(d 1) */ sq.dbid, sq.snap_id, sq.con_dbid, min(sq.instance_number) min_inst_num, sq.sql_id, plan_hash_value, sum(cpu_time_delta) cpu_time, sum(buffer_gets_delta) buffer_gets, sum(executions_delta) executions from awr_root_sqlstat sq, v$database d, awr_root_sqltext st where sq.dbid = d.dbid and st.dbid = sq.dbid and st.sql_id = sq.sql_id and st.con_dbid = sq.con_dbid and sq.snap_id between :bid and :eid and st.command_type in (2, 3, 6, 7, 189) and bitand(nvl(sq.flag, 0), 1) = 0 group by sq.dbid, sq.snap_id, sq.sql_id, sq.con_dbid, plan_hash_value)) where within_snap_rnk <= 150 ) v1, (select sq.sql_id, sq.con_dbid from awr_root_sqlstat sq, v$database d where sq.dbid = d.dbid and sq.snap_id be tween :bid and :eid group by sq.dbid, sq.sql_id, sq.con_dbid having sum(nvl(executions_delta, 0)) >= 2) v2 where v1.sql_id = v2.sql_id and v1.con_dbid = v2.con_dbid ) f, awr_root_snapshot s where f.snap_id = s.snap_id and f.dbid = s.dbid and s.instance_number = f.min_inst_num) group by grouping sets ((dbid, sql_id, con_dbid, plan_hash_value, snap_id), (dbid, sql_id, con_dbid, plan_hash_value, day_id), (dbid, sql_id, con_dbid, plan_hash_value, hour_id), (dbid, sql_id, con_dbid, plan_hash_value))))) group by dbid, sql_id, con_dbid, bucket_id) where cpu_plus_io >= decode(bucket_id, 0, (10 * 1000000), 1, (60 * 1000000), 2, (240 * 1000000), (480 * 1000000)))where within_buc ket_rnk <= 150) order by bucket_id asc, cpu_plus_io desc

  • SP: Shared Pool Est LC: Estimated Library Cache Factr: Factor

ADDM Task ADDM:1515833840_1_3858

          ADDM Report for Task 'ADDM:1515833840_1_3858'
          ---------------------------------------------

Analysis Period
---------------
AWR snapshot range from 3857 to 3858.
Time period starts at 11-MAR-19 09.30.16 PM
Time period ends at 11-MAR-19 10.30.23 PM

Analysis Target
---------------
Database 'ORCL' with DB ID 1515833840.
Database version 12.2.0.1.0.
ADDM performed an analysis of instance ORASHAFT, numbered 1 and hosted at
orcl.shaft.com.

Activity During the Analysis Period
-----------------------------------
Total database time was 380 seconds.
The average number of active sessions was .11.

Summary of Findings
-------------------
   Description                         Active Sessions      Recommendations
                                       Percent of Activity
   ----------------------------------  -------------------  ---------------
1  "User I/O" wait Class               .02 | 20.6           0
2  PGA_AGGREGATE_LIMIT Throttling      .02 | 17.02          1
3  Hard Parse Due to Sharing Criteria  .01 | 5.33           1
4  Commits and Rollbacks               0 | 3.97             1


~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~


          Findings and Recommendations
          ----------------------------

Finding 1: "User I/O" wait Class
Impact is .02 active sessions, 20.6% of total activity.
-------------------------------------------------------
Wait class "User I/O" was consuming significant database time.
The throughput of the I/O subsystem was not significantly lower than expected.

   No recommendations are available.


Finding 2: PGA_AGGREGATE_LIMIT Throttling
Impact is .02 active sessions, 17.02% of total activity.
--------------------------------------------------------
Database sessions were consuming significant PGA memory in some database
instances (or PDBs).

   Recommendation 1: Database Configuration
   Estimated benefit is .02 active sessions, 17.02% of total activity.
   -------------------------------------------------------------------
   Action
      Sessions were consuming significant PGA memory. Consider increasing the
      PGA limit for these sessions by increasing the value of the parameter
      PGA_AGGREGATE_LIMIT.

   Symptoms That Led to the Finding:
   ---------------------------------
      Wait class "Scheduler" was consuming significant database time.
      Impact is .02 active sessions, 17.02% of total activity.


Finding 3: Hard Parse Due to Sharing Criteria
Impact is .01 active sessions, 5.33% of total activity.
-------------------------------------------------------
SQL statements with the same text were not shared because of cursor
environment mismatch. This resulted in additional hard parses which were
consuming significant database time.
Common causes of environment mismatch are session NLS settings, SQL trace
settings and optimizer parameters.

   Recommendation 1: Application Analysis
   Estimated benefit is .01 active sessions, 5.33% of total activity.
   ------------------------------------------------------------------
   Action
      Look for top reason for cursor environment mismatch in
      V$SQL_SHARED_CURSOR.

   Symptoms That Led to the Finding:
   ---------------------------------
      Hard parsing of SQL statements was consuming significant database time.
      Impact is .01 active sessions, 7.61% of total activity.


Finding 4: Commits and Rollbacks
Impact is 0 active sessions, 3.97% of total activity.
-----------------------------------------------------
Waits on event "log file sync" while performing COMMIT and ROLLBACK operations
were consuming significant database time.

   Recommendation 1: Host Configuration
   Estimated benefit is 0 active sessions, 3.97% of total activity.
   ----------------------------------------------------------------
   Action
      Investigate the possibility of improving the performance of I/O to the
      online redo log files.
   Rationale
      The average size of writes to the online redo log files was 15 K and the
      average time per write was 6 milliseconds.
   Rationale
      The total I/O throughput on redo log files was 0 K per second for reads
      and 30 K per second for writes.
   Rationale
      The redo log I/O throughput was divided as follows: 0% by RMAN and
      recovery, 100% by Log Writer, 0% by Archiver, 0% by Streams AQ and 0% by
      all other activity.

   Symptoms That Led to the Finding:
   ---------------------------------
      Wait class "Commit" was consuming significant database time.
      Impact is 0 active sessions, 3.97% of total activity.

~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~

          Additional Information
          ----------------------

The optimal memory target for the instance could not be determined because of
incomplete AWR snapshots.

Wait class "Application" was not consuming significant database time.
Wait class "Concurrency" was not consuming significant database time.
Wait class "Configuration" was not consuming significant database time.
CPU was not a bottleneck for the instance.
Wait class "Network" was not consuming significant database time.
Session connect and disconnect calls were not consuming significant database
time.

The database's maintenance windows were active during 50% of the analysis
period.
